APPENDIX K
LIQUIDITY
A. Eager and deterministic strategies
We will assume that BitMLx strategies are eager meaning that a user will always schedule a contract action if it is possible.
This implies in particular that a user will schedule a skip ac tion whenever the priority action is ‚ÄĚblocked‚ÄĚ by another us er.
DeÔ¨Ānition 25 (Eager BitMLx strategies). A BitML x strategy ő£x
A is eager if the following condition holds:
‚ąÄRx. ő£x
A‚äĘ Rx‚áí‚ąÄ őļ‚ąą contracts(Rx) : (‚ąÉőĪ őďx : Rx őĪ (őļ )
‚ąí‚ąí‚ąí‚Üí őďx)‚áí‚ąÉ őĪ ‚Ä≤‚ąą ő£x
A(Rx)
‚ąß (‚ąÉ ňÜőĪ (őļ). ňÜőĪ (őļ) = őĪ ‚Ä≤ ‚ą® őĪ ‚Ä≤ = A : őļ
‚ą® (‚ü®reveal S then C +> D, B‚ü©őļ )‚ąą őďx ‚ąß őĪ ‚Ä≤ = A : a ‚ąß a‚ąą S)
‚ąß (‚ąÄőďx : Rx őĪ ‚Ä≤
‚ąí‚Üí őďx‚áí őďxŐł= őď x(Rx))
Note that this deÔ¨Ānition ensures that the honest user strate gy needs to eventually schedule skip actions (if possible) but at
the same time allows for scheduling other actions őĪ ‚Ä≤, e.g., authorizations or reveal secrets for enabling other (left) moves.
However, it is required that such őĪ ‚Ä≤ actions need to change conÔ¨Āgurations (this, in particular, forbids double authorizations).
In addition to strategies being eager, we will also require t hem to be deterministic. Intuitively, a strategy is deterministic if
will never schedule contradicting actions for the same cont ract.
DeÔ¨Ānition 26 (Deterministic BitMLx strategies). A BitML x strategy ő£x
A is deterministic if the following condition holds:
‚ąÄRx. ő£x

Note that ő£x
A being deterministic and persistent ensures in particular t hat it will never happen that ő£x
A schedules a skip(őļ)
action and then a lef t(őļ) action afterwards.
Determinism is from a security perspective a sensible requi rement on user strategies, since in cases of non-determinis m, it
is left to the (adversarial) scheduler to resolve non-deter minism.
Another requirement on x-strategies ő£x
A will be that those strategies will only propose and execute a Ô¨Ānite number of
contractsK. This requirement is needed since, technically it is not pre vented that an ő£x
A keeps on proposing (the same)
contracts over and over again. We will call such strategies t o be K-bounded.

C. Intermediate Liquidity
We will extend the notion of liquidity to the intermediate se mantics:
DeÔ¨Ānition 31 (Liquidated runs) . LetK be a set of contracts and R|| an intermediate run. Then R|| is liquidated if for all
‚ü®C, ŌÄ‚ü©B
őļ‚ąą őď||(R||) one of the following holds
‚ÄĘ ‚ąÉB : ŌÄ [status] = Assigned(B)
‚ÄĘ ‚ąÉB : ŌÄ [status] = Slashed(B)
‚ÄĘ ‚ąÉB : ŌÄ [status] = CompensatedFrom(B)
‚ÄĘ ‚ąÉB : ŌÄ [status] = Stip-Refunded(B)
‚ÄĘ ‚ąÉB : ŌÄ [status] = Stip-Slashed(B)
‚ÄĘ ‚ąÉB : ŌÄ [status] = Stip-Compensation(B)
W e deÔ¨Āne Liquidated-Status to be the set that includes every liquidated status.
DeÔ¨Ānition 32 (Strong Intermediate Liquidity) . Let A be an honest participant with strategy ő£||
A. Then ő£||
A is strongly liquid
if for all runs R|| there exists an extension ňÜR|| = R|| őĪ 1
‚ąí‚Üí¬∑¬∑¬∑

‚ąí‚ąí‚Üí such that

‚ąí‚Üí¬∑¬∑¬∑
őĪ i‚ąí 1
‚ąí‚ąí‚ąí‚Üí )

Note that the second condition accounts for the fact that the intermediate semantics does not delete contracts but chang es
their status to indicate that they have been executed until Ô¨Ā nalization.
We Ô¨Ārst deÔ¨Āne the liquidation distance of an intermediate ru n R||. The liquidation distance is a measure of how close an
intermediate run is to liquidation. Intuitively, an interm ediate run will always be liquidated because its contracts ( on all chains)
will either (1) terminate regularly or (2) will be compensat ed.
To ensure liquidation, we need to consider the honest user st rategy ő£||
A to be bounded by a set of contracts K, meaning
that ő£||
A only proposes contracts from K and at most once. Otherwise, the strategy could continue adv ertising new contracts
without ever agreeing on time to pass.
This property should be inherited from the underlying ő£x
A. For this reason,
DeÔ¨Ānition 33 (Liquidation Distance) . Let A be an honest participant with strategy ő£||
A andK a set of contracts such that
ő£||
A isK-bounded. The liquidation distance of an intermediate run R|| w.r .t. to ő£||

Intuitively, the different components forming the liquida tion distance have the following meaning:
‚ÄĘ K‚ąí denotes the set of contracts őļ 0 fromK which have not been advertised yet.
‚ÄĘ C‚ąí
adv denotes the set of advertised contracts őļ 0 that are still lacking commitments (from user A).
‚ÄĘ A‚ąí
adv denotes the set of advertised contracts and blockchains (őļ 0,
B) that are still lacking authorizations (from user A).
Note that authorizations are carried out per blockchain B.
‚ÄĘ őīadv denotes the set of advertised contracts and blockchains (őļ 0, B) that have not been published yet. Note that contracts
őļ 0 need to be published individually on each blockchain.
‚ÄĘ S‚ąí
stip denotes the set of published contracts őļ 0 that are still lacking the init secrets (from user A). Note that there is a
single init secret per contract őļ 0 and user that honest A will only release once the contract őļ 0 has been published on all
chains.
‚ÄĘ őīstip-status
B denotes the set of contracts, blockchain with their corresp onding stipulation status (őļ 0, B, status). Note that a
contract őļ 0 might be in different stages of stipulation (indicated by status) on the different blockchains
‚ÄĘ Dstip-phase
B denotes the set of contracts with their corresponding stipu lation phase (őļ 0, p ).
‚ÄĘ DES denotes the set of all running contracts with their Ô¨Ānalizat ion distance (őļ, n ), which is given by the depth of the
contract. Note that since contracts are non-recursive, the maximal number of execution steps is bounded by the contract
structure.
‚ÄĘ S‚ąí
ES denotes the set of all running contracts őļ that are missing a step secret from A.
‚ÄĘ Dsync
B denotes the set of running contracts, blockchains and their synchronization distance (őļ, B, n ). The synchronization
distance n denotes how far the contract őļ on blockchain B is lacking behind its furthest descendant (on any other chai n).
‚ÄĘ A‚ąí
B denotes the set of running (priority choice) contracts and b lockchains (őļ,
B) that are still lacking authorizations from
A.
‚ÄĘ őīstatus
B denotes the set of running contracts, blockchains and their execution stats (őļ, B, status). Note that a contract őļ may
be in different stages of execution on the different blockch ains.
‚ÄĘ S‚ąí
reveal denotes the set of running contracts their secrets that need to be revealed (őļ, s ).

‚ÄĘ Dround
B denotes the set of running contracts, blockchains and the co rresponding execution round and phase Ô¨Ānalization
distances (őļ, someBlockchain, r őī, p őī). Here, rőī denotes the number of rounds that need to pass until executio n of őļ will
be latest enforced and pőī denotes the phase within the enforcement round.
